| ہم وہ ہیں کہ اللہ نے کوثر ہمیں بخشا | سرداری فردوس کا افسر ہمیں بخشا |
| --- | --- |
| قوت دی ہیں، زور ہمیں نور ہمیں بخشا | اقبال علی، خُلق پیمبر ہمیں بخشا |
| ہم نور ہیں گھر طور تجلی ہے ہمارا | تخت دن داؤد مُصَلاَّ ہے ہمارا |
| واللہ ! وہ ہر ایک خلد میں عرفاں ہیں تو ہم ہیں! | کونین میں گر صادق ایماں ہیں تو ہم ہیں! |
| محسن ہیں تو ہم ! صاحب احساں ہیں تو ہم ہیں! | بھیجا جسے خالق نے وہ قرآن ہیں تو ہم ہیں! |
| گھر علم خدا کا ہے سفینے میں ہمارے ! | تفسیر میں کب ہے، جو ہے سینوں میں ہمارے! |

<!-- section 13 (id=1042, raw_sort=13): وکل شئی احصینہ فی امام مبین -->
امام کی عظمت کو واضح کرتے ہوئے اللہ تعالی ارشاد فرماتا ہے:

> ⟪quran 36:12⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنَّا نَحْنُ نُحْىِ ٱلْمَوْتَىٰ وَنَكْتُبُ مَا قَدَّمُوا۟ وَآثَرَهُمْۚ وَكُلَّ شَىْءٍ أَحْصَيْنَهُ فِىٓ إِمَامٍۢ مُّبِينٍۢ ‎⟫
> *Verily, We give life to the dead, and We record that which they send before (them), and their traces [their footsteps and walking on the earth with their legs to the mosques for the five compulsory congregational prayers, Jihad (holy fighting in Allah's Cause) and all other good and evil they did, and that which they leave behind], and all things We have recorded with numbers (as a record) in a Clear Book.*
> بے شک ہم ہی مردوں کو زندہ کریں گے اور جو انھوں نے آگے بھیجا اور جو پیچھے چھوڑا اس کو لکھتے ہیں اور ہم نے ہر چیز کو کتاب واضح [لوح محفوظ] میں محفوظ کر رکھا ہے
> — **Quran 36:12 (inline widget)**

⟪ar:امیر المؤمنین علی ابن ابی طالب⟫نے انسان کو ⟪ar:عالم الکبیر⟫کہا ہے۔ مولانا علی فرماتے ہیں کہ انسان میں اللہ تعالی نے پورے عالم کو پوشیدہ کیا ہے۔ اس میں چاند اور سورج جیسی روشن آنکھیں ہیں، اس میں چاروں عناصر (آگ، ہوا، پانی، مٹی) پائے جاتے ہیں۔ اس کے جسم میں پہاڑ کی اونچائیاں اور غار کی گہرائیاں ہیں۔ اس کے جسم میں خون کی نہریں بہتی ہیں۔ نہ صرف یہ بلکہ انسان نے معدن نبات اور حیوان کو اپنے حکم کے تابع کیا ہوا ہے۔ جب انسان کی یہ حالت ہے اور ہم مانتے ہیں کہ امام انسانوں سے بہت افضل ہیں، تو پھر اس امام کی کیا شان ہوگی؟ اس کے حکم کے تابع تو کائنات اور اس میں رہنے والے تمام انس و جن ہیں۔

اس آیت سے صاف ظاہر ہے کہ امام کی ذات انسانوں سے بہت افضل اور الگ ہے ۔ انسانوں میں اور ان میں کوئی نسبت نہیں ہے۔ اور یہ بھی کہ وہ اپنے عصر میں مالک وقت ہے، اور ہر چیز اس کے حکم کے تابع ہے۔ اولیاء اللہ نے اس آیت میں ایک اور باریک نقطہ یہ نکالا ہے کہ جو لوگ بھی ترقی کر کے امام کے ⟪ar:لاہوت و ناست⟫میں شامل ہو گئے، وہی حقیقت میں ⟪ar:شئی⟫(کام کی چیز) بن گئے۔ ان کے مقابل میں باقی تمام ⟪ar:لا شئی⟫(بے کار چیزیں) ہیں جن کی کوئی وقعت نہیں۔

<!-- section 14 (id=1435, raw_sort=14): کتاب الاثبات الامامۃ -->
## The Importance of Imams

**In the Name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful.**

All praise is for Allah, who sent prophets and appointed Imams and caliphs to guide His creation. I bear witness that there is no God but Allah, and that Muhammad is His servant and messenger. May Allah bless him, his family, and his companion Ali, who is the most knowledgeable in the interpretation of the Quran.

The Imamate is the foundation of religion; all matters revolve around it. It is the source of knowledge of Allah and the Quran. The Imamate is affirmed through evidence and deduction. Those who came before have written on the topic of the affirmation of Imamate, citing evidence from the Quran and the Prophet's traditions. The necessity of having an Imam is essential in natural disposition, innate constitution, nature, intellect, governance, prescription, and norms. It is obligatory in all revealed laws, religions, and religious communities, just as the existence of a Creator is necessary.   

People of different religions call their past Imams prophets and sages. Some misguided Muslims call their scholars and jurists Imams. Whoever wants salvation must lay aside his inclinations and desires and comprehend the deficiency in every false pretender for the esteemed designation of Imam.

We shall now mention some of the weaknesses of those who falsely claim Imamate. Then, we will turn their principles against them and repudiate the Imamate from those not suited for it. We will establish the Imamate of the true Imams with proofs and demonstrations. We will also show the necessity of obeying them, entrusting our affairs to their command, and accepting the revelation, interpretation, and confession of unity from them.   

Allah, through His wisdom and power, created the human body with its senses, and its sustenance through which it survives. Similarly, He made principles, causes, and means for the souls, spirits, and noetic forms through which they acquire their spiritual sustenance, nourishment, and survival.

The differences in the degrees of excellence that exist among all entities comprising the essence and their derivations are the firmest evidence and proof of affirming the Imamate and the Imams. Allah created entities in all genera and species, different and disparate from each other in respect to their excellence. He made those genera and species either a necessity for humans without which their physical existence and function would not be complete, or a source of nourishment, a medicine, an elegance, an adornment, and an indispensable tool for their existence.   

The necessity of the Imam is clear from the differences and degrees of excellence that exist among all entities. The summit in each genus and species points to the Imam. The following table illustrates this:

| Category | Noblest of the Category | Points to the Imam |
| --- | --- | --- |
| The Ten Categories | The essence (جوھر) upon which all others rest.  1 | The permanent, intellectual, luminous, authentic substance (جوھر الحقیقی النوری العقلی الأبدی) through which all souls are illumined.  2 |
| The Four Basic Constituents | Heat, from which arises luminosity, light, motion, movement, and elevation.  3 | The Imam, from whom comes intellectual light (النور العقلی), motion (الحرکۃ), and elevation (العلو).  4 |
| The Celestial Spheres | The outermost sphere (فلک الافلاک المحیط) in which they all orbit.  5 | The Imam, who is the supreme religious sphere for all other spheres.  6 |
| The Four Elements | Fire, which is the summit and peak.  7 | The Imam, who is the highest religious pillar that illumines souls.  8 |
| Planets | The Sun, through which all plants, animals, and newborns grow and become perfect.  9 | The Imam, who is the Sun of religion through which souls are illumined from the light of guidance and wisdom.  10 |
| Signs of the Zodiac | The fourth sign of the zodiac.  11 | The fourth proof (حجۃ), who is directly connected to the Imam (باب الابواب).  12 |
| The Climes | The fourth clime.  13 | The Imam, who is the fourth and most excellent of the proofs (حجۃ).  14 |
| Melting Mineral Substances | Gold, with which people conduct their business.  15 | The Imam, through whom the worldly and religious transactions of creation and their well-being are completed.  16 |
| Grains | Wheat, which is the most balanced in nature and nobility.  17 | The Imam, who benefits the souls and nourishes them with his knowledge.  18 |
| Fruit-bearing Trees | The date palm tree, in which everything is beneficial and nothing is wasted.  19 | The Imam, who is the head and leader of all believers.  20 |
| Medicinal Plants | The medicines that cure chronic diseases and are antidotes for those on the verge of death.  21 | The Imam, whose words are antidotes for the souls.  22 |
| Animals | The horse, the eagle, and the lion, who are the best among their species.  23 | The Imam, who is the peak and summit of the human species.  24 |
| Plants | The sweet, pleasant plants that people benefit from.  25 | The Imams, who are a symbol of their speech and knowledge that entice the soul and please the eyes.  26 |
| Animals That Produce Musk and Honey | The gazelle that gives musk and the bees that provide honey.  27 | The Imam, who is the chief of believers. |

 [1] Praise be to Allah, who sent messengers and prophets and appointed Imams and caliphs as a blessing for His friends (اولیا); a punishment for His enemies; a benefit for His religion and His world, as well as being an edifice (a complex system of beliefs.) (عمارت) for the present world and the world hereafter. I praise Him with the eulogy of one who is aware of the immense value of the bounty brought forth through them, and who is grateful for it and who fares (travels) his way for the sake of Allah, hastening towards it. I bear witness that there is no deity (الہ) except Allah, with the testimony of a worshipper who is aware of the requirements of this obligation, and who strives to fulfil it. I also bear witness that Muhammad (PBUH) is His slave (عبدہ) and Messenger (ورسولہ). Who is preferred over all His messengers and is immune from all mistakes and errors. May Allah bless him with innumerable and infinite blessings. May Allah also bless his loyal and truthful legatee (وصی) Ali Ibn Abu Talib (AS), who is adept in the clarification of the spiritual realities hidden in the Holy Quran. May He also bless the Imams that descended from the progeny of the martyr, to whom belong praise, glory, infallibility and uprightness. May He also bless the master of the palace and age (Imam Al-Hakim Be Amr Allah), who was supported by conquest and victory. May the most excellent salutations of Allah, and the most bounteous blessings and purest greetings be upon him and on the heir-apparent of the Muslims (ولی العہد المسلمین) and the vicegerent (خلیفۃ) of the Commander of the Faithful, as long as tongues discourse and darkness and light continue to alternate. And now...

[2] The Imamate is the pole (قطب) and foundation of religion (اساس الدین) around which all religious and worldly matters revolve. It is a benefit for this present life and the life hereafter. It governs the affairs of the worshippers, the prosperity of the land and the acceptance of recompense in the abode of return (دار الأخرۃ). It is through imamate that knowledge of Allah’s absolute unity (توحید) and of the revealed Message is attained. This knowledge is based on proof, demonstration and evidence; as is the knowledge of the religious law, its foundation and its interpretation (تاویل) and clarification.

[3] We have said that the imamate is the pole and foundation of religion, but we have not given precedence to prophethood (رسالت) over the imamate. This is because in the affirmation of imamate, there is an affirmation of the prophethood. Whoever acknowledges the imam, also acknowledges the messenger. But not all those who acknowledge the messenger acknowledge the reality of the Imam. Proof of prophethood is required for those who are outside the domain of Islam, while affirming the imamate is necessary for Muslims (مسلمین) who are closer to the true believers (مؤمنین). The struggle required with them, through debate and argument, has priority over those denying the messenger and the prophethood. This is because the summon to Islam and the prophethood has reached the polytheists and a proof has already been established for them. Hence confronting them (Muslims) with the sword is more appropriate as the world can never be deprived of an imam at any given moment or time, while the messenger is present at certain times but not at others. Therefore, in affirming the imamate, there is also an affirmation of the prophethood!

Allah, the Exalted, called the imam a messenger when He said:

‏وَٱذْكُرْ فِى ٱلْكِتَبِ إِسْمَعِيلَ ۚ إِنَّهُۥ كَانَ صَادِقَ ٱلْوَعْدِ وَكَانَ رَسُولًۭا نَّبِيًّۭا ‎

 And remember in the Scripture Ismaeel was indeed faithful in fulfilling his promise while he was a messenger, a prophet.

Likewise, Allah called the messenger Ibrahim, an "Imam" when he had completed his prophethood. He said:

‏ وَإِذِ ٱبْتَلَىٰٓ إِبْرَهِمَ رَبُّهُۥ بِكَلِمَتٍۢ فَأَتَمَّهُنَّ ۖ قَالَ إِنِّى جَاعِلُكَ لِلنَّاسِ إِمَامًۭا.....  قَالَ وَمِن ذُرِّيَّتِى ۖ قَالَ لَا يَنَالُ عَهْدِى ٱلظَّلِمِينَ ‎

124 اور جب ابراھیم کو اس کے رب نے کئی باتوں میں آزمایا تو اس نےانہیں پورا کر دیا فرمایا بے شک میں تمہیں سب لوگوں کا پیشوا بنادوں گا کہا اور میری اولاد میں سے بھی فرمایا میرا عہد ظالموں کو نہیں پہنچے گا

It is related from Imam Ja’far al-Sadiq, peace be upon him, that he said ‘Allah chose Ibrahim as a prophet (نبی), then as a friend (خلیل), then as a messenger (رسول) and finally said: “I am appointing you an imam for all humanity’. Allah called Adam a vicegerent (خلیفۃ), and the name ‘vicegerent’ is one of the names of the imams. Allah called Dawood, peace be upon him, a vicegerent while he was one of the imams in the past cycles and called the proofs (حجۃ) "Prophets". He called Muhammad and other messengers "prophets" (نبی),  just as He addressed them as "messengers" (رسول). This is because the messenger arrives first at the rank of the imamate. Then, if the times requires the establishment of a new religious law, he becomes the seventh imam of that cycle, undertaking the promulgation of the religious law. Thus the Imam occupies the place of the messenger in his age and time. The messenger, before arising to promulgate the religious law, is one of the imams, having assumed command from a previous imam. After finalizing the religious law, he hands over the command to the next imam. The imam is therefore present in the world at all times; the world is never deprived of him. The imam supports and maintains the religious laws and its esoteric reality as we mentioned [earlier]. It is now clear that the progression of the religious cycle depends on the imam and that it is the imam’s prerogative how he acts on the prophet’s law during his time. No one can reach the prophet, nor attain his rank, or arrive at the proper understanding of the religious law, which is only changed or replaced by the imam. It is only through the imam that one can attain the inner truth of the religious law, its interpretation and meaning.

[5] Much work that is written on affirming the imamate by the elders of the da’wa, draw on deduction and evidence cited from well-known Quranic verses, that were revealed verifying the imamate and the imams, peace be upon them, in addition to traditions reported from the Prophet. Those who came before have left out nothing on this subject for those who came later, and there is no point in repeating the same notions in different words. Therefore, we wish to write a treaty on affirming the Imamate using evidence (استشھاد) and deduction (استدلال) from the [outer] horizons (الافق) and [our] inner selves (النفوس), from politics or governance (سیاسۃ) and norms (رسوم) by way of intellect (عقل), self-evidence (ضرورۃ), innate constitution (الفترۃ), natural disposition (الجِبِلَّۃ), and agreement (الاتفاق) from all religious communities (اہل کل ملۃ), as well as from philosophers (الفلاسفۃ) and mathematicians (اہل الحساب). We shall further deduce evidence from the structure of religious duties (فرائض) and practices in a way that has not been done by the elders of the da’wa. If my efforts are found reasonable, they are due to the excellence of support from the master of the age and the time (والی الامر والزمان). But, if there is any error, it is solely due to my [own] weakness and shortcoming, and that is most proper of me.

[6] Thus we say: Indeed the necessity (وجب) of the imamate and the imams, peace be upon them, is  essential in natural disposition (جبلۃ), and innate constitution (الفترۃ), in nature (التبیعۃ), intellect (عقل), governance (سیاسۃ), prescription (وضع) and norms (رسوم). It is obligatory in all revealed law (الشریعۃ), religion and religious communities, just as the existence of a Creator is necessary in innate constitution, natural disposition, and the intellect in every religious community and religion. But people differed regarding the Creator, after His necessity was proved, and after having accepted His existence. They began drawing conclusions according to their own personal whims and opinions as well as blindly imitating their forefathers and teachers, claiming that the Creator, who the innate constitution and natural disposition necessitates, is actually either a substance or elements or stars, or sun or something other than that. At times, they described the Creator with attributes that constitute His similarity that is, anthropomorphism (التجسُّم) or that which is similar to polytheism (شرک), basing those claims on their judgement without any authentic knowledge. Likewise, with regard to the necessity of the imamate, they fell into disagreement after their commitment to the imam. Some insisted that the imam, who is ascertained by intellect and self evidence, is the wise man of every age. This belief was similar to the views of philosophers who call their teachers ‘imams’, ‘sages’ (حکما), ‘head of the scholars’ (راس العلما), ‘master of the world’ (sã’is) and ‘the teacher’ (المعلمون).

[7] Followers of all religions called their past imams ‘prophets’ and ‘sages’ in every cycle (ادوار). However, certain misguided followers of Islam called usurpers, oppressive false pretenders, even their scholars and jurists, ‘imams’. Yet, if you examine their beliefs closely, they all confirm the existence of the imam simply by necessity (ضرورۃ), and are unable to deny His existence. Whoever wants salvation and guidance must lay aside his inclinations and desires and comprehend the deficiency in every false pretender for this esteemed designation. For such a pretender lacks in knowledge, gnosis or cognition, piety and all other merits and conditions of the imamate. The seeker of salvation, by realizing the pretender’s lack of knowledge and the triviality of his piety,  modesty and his inability to fulfil any of the conditions of the imamate, denies his imamate, until the time he attains recognition of the true imam (معرفت امام الحق).

[8] We shall now mention statements from every pretender identifying their weaknesses and limitations. We shall then turn their own principles against them, and repudiate (refuse to accept or be associated with) the imamate from those not suited for it. We shall establish the imamate of the true imams, peace be upon them, with proofs and demonstrations. We shall also establish the necessity of obeying them, entrusting our affairs to their command and accepting the revelation, the interpretation and the confession of unity (توحید) from them. All those who recognize the creation, realize their own inability and deficiency as creatures. They are forced to deny their own divinity, and thus the divinity of all created beings. Divine unity is then left pure, without ascription (attribution of something to a cause) of human qualities to Allah (تشبیح), and the denial of all attributes to Allah (تعتیل).

[9] We also say that Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) through His subtle wisdom and extensive power, created for the human body: principles (اصول), causes (علت) and means (اسباب). He manifested in all his derivatives (فروع), realms of nature (موالید مبروزۃ), and their traces, in a predetermined manner and in a definite term. He then brought forth from them a body with senses, parallel and corresponding to its principles. He made those principles and means its sustenance and nourishment through which he survives, and from which his physical and perceptual reward and punishment are determined. Similarly, He made principles, causes and means for the souls (نفوس), spirits (أرواح) and religious noetic forms (of or relating to mental activity or the intellect), through which they aquire their spiritual sustenance, nourishment and survival. They are rewarded when they adhere to them, and punished when they disrupt their support and distance them from their origin.

[10] Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) made the principles (اصول) and causes (علت) of the body, a testimony and proof for principles of the soul; as well as for its derivatives and its nourishment, so that the religious creation would be similar to, corresponding and parallel to the physical creation. The body manifests its perfection only through the effects of the celestial spheres along with the stars (کواکب). Without the stars, the body could not have achieved perfection simply through the celestial spheres, because the course of events are always influenced by the stars. Similarly the manifestation of the religious noetic forms and the everlasting souls manifest themselves and achieve perfection only through the influence of the Imams (peace be upon them). Their nourishment is from the imam's knowledge, because the imams are the religious stars. The Prophet (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) said: ‘My companions are like the stars - whichever you emulate (imitate), you will be guided. This holds true even when they act in place of the prophets who are like the celestial spheres. Thus, the course of affairs for all created beings, as well as their recourse is towards the Imams.

[11] We say that the differences in the degrees of excellence (⟪ar:التفاوت التفاضل⟫) that exist among all entities comprising of the essence (⟪ar:أصول⟫) and their derivations (⟪ar:فروع⟫) are the firmest evidence and proof of affirming the imamate and the imams. This is because Allah the exalted created entities in all genre (⟪ar:اجناس⟫) and species (⟪ar:انواع⟫), different and disparate from each other in respect to their excellence. He thereafter set for each and every genus and species an upper limit (⟪ar:غایۃ⟫), a summit (⟪ar:ذرورۃ⟫), an end (⟪ar:نھایۃ⟫) and a virtue (⟪ar:فضیلۃ⟫), which none other in that category can attain. He made those genera and species, either a necessity for humans without which their physical existence and function would not be complete; or alternatively, a source of nourishment, a medicine, an elegance, an adornment and an indispensable tool for their existence. He thus placed in all things a unique advantage (⟪ar:منفعۃ⟫) that does not exist in anything else (ecological niche). He powerfully endowed in them a capacity which the creation would necessarily and unavoidably need, and would not be able to continue its physical affairs without it (such as food and water). He also put them to a test by creating in them a 'need' (hunger and thirst) so that they are forced to seek and acquire those requirements in order to remove their need. Thus, when one cannot find the cure of that neediness in its place, he seeks it elsewhere and hastens to the place where it may be found. As long as one remains in this physical world, he cannot, even for a moment, dispense with breathing (التنسم) and seeking to benefit from the elements of this world, its derivations, realms of nature, vegetation and nourishment, all of which are a wisdom from Allah, the Exalted, and a mark of justice from Him. This is so that these aspects would serve as a witnesses and ephemeral, obligatory symbols (و مثالات جبریات) for the symbolized realities (ممثولات) that are religious, eternal and chosen. The benefit of all symbolized realities comprising principles, realms of nature, nourishment and religious remedies are more deserving, more worthy and more powerful than the obligatory symbols. Their need is more than the need of what is compulsory by nature because their benefits only affect the body while those of the symbolized realities affect the spirit and the soul. Therefore, the extent of increase in merit of the intellectual symbolized realities over the natural symbols is according to the extent of the spirits merit over the body. Furthermore, the merit of the symbolized over the symbol is according to the extent of the merit of the everlasting ones over the perishable ones. The merit in each one of them reflects the deficiency in the other. For whoever is deprived of the physical aspects he is in need of, will not experience destruction because of that. And even if there is a destruction, it would only be that of his body which undoubtedly will one day perish and die. However, in the absence of the symbolized, religious realities, there would be destruction of the soul, which plunges into perpetual punishment. Therefore, if people’s struggle in seeking for what the soul needs was similar to their struggle and desire for seeking what the body needs, then none would doubt, stray or ascribe human qualities to Allah, that is, anthropomorphism (⟪ar:تشبیح⟫).

[12] All of Allah's creation and their need are an admonition for the sake of the symbolized religious reality. It is a witness to everyone who seeks testimony for it and an evidence for whoever asks for such a proof. It is an insight for all those who see and reflect on it. It is also a proof against those who deny the symbolized religious reality of the imams and the hierarchies, as well as their knowledge and benefit - because they accept proofs of the benefit from natural elements, planets and the celestial spheres. Indeed Allah, the Exalted, has created these elements, means and natural causes as such powerful evidence, that no one is able to deny them or seek testimony against them, change or alter them, unlike what they have done with the religious law and with what the Prophet had asked them to bear witness to, concerning affirmation of the imamate and the imams—its necessity and devotion to the imams, the necessity of obeying them, condemning those who disobey them, and promising reward to those who obey them—and in a manner in which they changed the Quran and distorted it.  As Allah, the Exalted says:
⟪ar-quote:يُحَرِّفُونَ ٱلْكَلِمَ عَن مَّوَاضِعِهِۦ ۙ وَنَسُوا۟ حَظًّۭا مِّمَّا ذُكِّرُوا۟ بِهِ⟫

They change words from their context while they forgot a portion of what We have reminded them of’

and Allah also states:
⟪ar-quote:إِنَّمَا ٱلنَّسِىٓءُ زِيَادَةٌۭ فِى ٱلْكُفْرِ⟫

indeed, forgetfulness is only an excess of disbelief

That was not forgetfulness on their part. because they forgot the testimony intentionally as though they had neither seen nor heard it

[13] Furthermore, just as the testimony of the outer horizons (⟪ar:آفاق⟫) and the inner selves (⟪ar:انفس⟫) are compulsory (⟪ar:جبری⟫) and not voluntary (⟪ar:اختیاری⟫), making it impossible for anyone to either alter or substitute it; likewise the Messenger, may Allah bless him, made the testimony compulsory; without entailing a choice for the witnesses to change, alter or conceal it. He has threatened whoever would attempt to change or conceal it with a painful punishment. Allah, the Exalted, ordered [man] to judge on the basis of the testimony of two witnesses, mentioning in His words:
⟪ar-quote:أَن تَضِلَّ إِحْدَهُمَا فَتُذَكِّرَ إِحْدَهُمَا ٱلْأُخْرَىٰ وَلَا يَأْبَ ٱلشُّهَدَآءُ إِذَا مَا دُعُوا۟⟫

If one of them falls into error the other will remind. And the witnesses must not refuse when they are summoned.

By this, He meant that true judgement in religion and in affirming the imamate and the hierarchies is at the hands of two witnesses, one posited by law (⟪ar:شرعی⟫) and the other compelled by nature (⟪ar:طبعی⟫). If people deny the legally established testimony, then the one bound by nature, namely the horizons and our [own] innerselves reminds, enforces and verifies the conventional witnesses, just as Allah, the Exalted, says:
⟪ar-quote:سَنُرِيهِمْ آيَتِنَا فِى ٱلأٓفَاقِ وَفِىٓ أَنفُسِهِمْ حَتَّىٰ يَتَبَيَّنَ لَهُمْ أَنَّهُ ٱلْحَقُّ ۗ أَوَلَمْ يَكْفِ بِرَبِّكَ أَنَّهُۥ عَلَىٰ كُلِّ شَىْءٍۢ شَهِيدٌ⟫

‘We shall show them our signs on the horizons and within themselves until it becomes manifest to them that it is the Truth

And just as the Prophet, when asked, Who is the witness of your prophethood?’ answered: ⟪ar:یشھد لی کل حجر و مدر⟫ [My witness is every stone and every piece of clay]. His words pointed to the testimony of the horizons and the souls. Thus, when legal (⟪ar:شرعی⟫) and natural (⟪ar:طبعی⟫) witnesses testify, and intellect becomes the criterion in assessing the witnesses without preference or partiality then truth swiftly becomes manifest.

[14] Now, we shall mention the differences and degrees of excellence in each principle (⟪ar:اصل⟫) and realm of nature (⟪ar:موالید⟫). We shall also show that the ultimate limit and highest summit in each genus and species points to the imam in every age and time.

[15] The sages (⟪ar:حکما⟫) among the philosophers mention the ten categories and say that one cannot mention or discuss anything except in reference to these ten:

'Essence' (⟪ar:جوھر⟫) is the ultimate, upon which all others rest and which excels over all others because the remaining nine are established from it. Therefore, the essence that they describe, is a proof for the permanent, intellectual, luminous and authentic substance (جوھر الحقیقی النوری العقلی الأبدی) through which all souls are illumined and on which all nine depend. Yet, it is one that has no need of any created thing; it draws benefit from nothing or no one in the world, but rather, everything benefits from it and is in need of it. That is the Imam, peace be upon him! All other ranks are below him just as the nine categories are in respect to the ‘essence’

[16] We also say that among the four basic Constituents (⟪ar:العناثر⟫) from which the first composites (⟪ar:ترکیب⟫) were composed, two are active and two passive. The two active ones are heat and cold while the two passive ones are dryness and humidity. The ultimate and the noblest among them is heat, from which arises luminosity, light, motion, movement and elevation while the other three are established through it. Heat thus has precedence in origin and in existence. No foundation or realm of nature would be complete without it. Likewise, the Imam illumines the soul and from Him comes intellectual light (النور العقلی), motion (الحرکۃ) and elevation (العلو). No principle or religious realm is complete without him. Additionally, among the celestial spheres, the most lofty and supreme sphere is the outermost one (فلک الافلاک المحیط) in which they all orbit. Likewise, the imam in His religion is the supreme religious sphere for all other spheres. All heavenly bodies and religious signs of the zodiac function under his command. If someone were to claim that this is rather a symbol for the Qayam (resurrector), given that the highest principle in the world points to the intellect in respect to the four principles, then we would reply that the imam is the Qayam of his time. He is the proclaimer (الناطق) in his age and time, and he is the one who assumes the position of the partial Qayam (⟪ar:جزوی⟫). The imam’s position in his realm is that of the Universal Intellect (العقل الکلی).

[17] We also say that among the four elements (⟪ar:الارکان⟫), the highest and the noblest is fire which is the summit and peak, to which no other element or nature can attain. Likewise, the imam, in his age and time, is the highest religious pillar that illuminates souls. On this basis Ibrahim (PBUH) ordered glorification of the fire (if what has been reported from him is true), preventing them from extinguishing and puffing it out. However, the indication was towards glorifying the imamate, which no one must put out through the injustice of those who falsely claim its position. The fire worshippers fell into confusion, not knowing its symbolized reality. Allah, the Exalted, related about the adversaries and the usurpers of the position of the Imamate in his words:
⟪ar-quote:يُرِيدُونَ أَن يُطْفِـُٔوا۟ نُورَ ٱللَّهِ بِأَفْوَهِهِمْ وَيَأْبَى ٱللَّهُ إِلَّآ أَن يُتِمَّ نُورَهُۥ وَلَوْ كَرِهَ ٱلْكَفِرُونَ⟫

'They would like to extinguish Allah’s light with their mouths, but Allah will not allow that [to happen] until He perfects His light even if the unbelievers may detest it'

[18] We also maintain that there are many planets (⟪ar:کواکب⟫), and among them there are differences and disparities in degrees of excellence. Their peak and summit in nobility and merit is the sun through which physical eyesight draws its light, and through which all plants, animals and newborns grow and become perfect. No plant or newborn can grow without the effect of the sun. Likewise the Imam is the sun of religion through which insight is enlightened and souls are illumined from the light of guidance and wisdom, radiating the hearts of Allah’s friends.

It is because of this that some people propose to glorify the sun. However, worshippers of the sun too fell into confusion as they only recognized the symbol, and not the symbolized reality. It is for this reason the Prophet, may Allah bless him, indicated the rising of the sun from the west which signals the rising of the Imam (Mehdi), peace be upon him, in the Maghrib. If the physical sun were to depart from its usual orbit and its ascent and descent from its centre, for even a blink of an eye, the entire world would be destroyed; which is impossible to happen, both rationally and naturally. Therefore, the Prophet’s statement could only hold true on the basis of esoteric interpretation. In fact, his interpretation has proved accurate as we have witnessed it with our own eyes by the grace and favour of Allah.

[19] We also say that among the twelve signs of the zodiac, four are most glorious and excellent. One of those four is the peak and the summit in nobility Likewise, among the twelve proofs (⟪ar:حجۃ⟫), the one who is directly connected to the Imam (⟪ar:باب الابواب⟫) is the most excellent, the noblest and the most exalted of them all.

[20] We maintain that the fourth clime[A region considered with reference to its climate] (⟪ar:أقلیم⟫), which is parallel to the fourth heaven and parallel to the sun, is the most moderate as well as being the most excellent and noblest of all. Similarly the imam is the most excellent in the hierarchy as well as the most glorious of them all, being their peak and apex. Four is emphasized in the four elements, seasons, humours and directions.

[21] We also say that among the melting mineral substances the most excellent is gold. It is that with which people conduct their business. It establishes the value of valuables; is not affected by fire or water; nor does it get destroyed. Likewise the Imam, peace of Allah be upon him, is the most excellent religious and intellectual substance in his age and time. Through him the worldly and religious transactions of the creation and their well-being are completed.

Each melting substance has its peak in nobility. Among these precious stones, the best is sapphire (⟪ar:الیاقوت⟫), and among all  the white, green, yellow and red sapphires (⟪ar:یاقوت الاحمر⟫), it is the red ruby which is excellent. No other jewel lasts like the ruby, because it maintains its essence and does not get transformed by fire or water; it always retains its purity, radiance and gravity. It obtains traces from its source in a manner that no other substances can. Not even other sapphires (⟪ar:یاقوت⟫), emeralds (⟪ar:الزمرد⟫), the carnelian (⟪ar:البیجاد⟫), agate (⟪ar:العقیق⟫), diamonds (⟪ar:والألماس⟫), turquoise (⟪ar:والفروزج⟫), are able retain these qualities. So the crown among the jewels is the red ruby just as the Imam is the peak amongst all creation of his age and time in his excellence. He is unique among all the ranks of the hierarchy—among the proofs (⟪ar:حجۃ⟫), the adjuncts (⟪ar:لواحق⟫), the summoner (⟪ar:داعی⟫), the wing (⟪ar:جناح⟫), the licensee (⟪ar:ماذون⟫) and the motivator (⟪ar:مکلب⟫)’

Therefore  no one is able to attain the status, rank or position of the Imam in His age or time. From a different perspective, the seven jewels are proofs for the seven ‘proclaimers’ (⟪ar:النطقا⟫) and the seven imams. The natural symbol is present in every age and time, and therefore the symbolized reality ought to be present in every age and time as well. Just as the stars, the natural elements, the realms of nature and the substances are present in all times; similarly the ranks of the hierarchy also must exist in every age and time so that they always influence the souls.

[22] We maintain that there are seven grains that provide human beings with food and nourishment. Their peak and summit is wheat, which is the most balanced in nature and nobility and which helps build the body. Likewise it is the Imam who is the peak and summit, who benefits the souls and nourishes them with his knowledge. He is the source of their spiritual livelihood and life.

[23] As for the fruit-bearing trees, the peak and summit among them is the date palm tree. It shares a similar trait to human beings by having a male and female gender, and who mates and impregnates like the animals. In addition, everything in the date palm is beneficial and nothing is wasted; its fruit is eaten at all times, be it raw or cooked. The interpretation of the dream that one is plucking dates from a date palm, is that he is going to benefit from a certain believer. That believer in reality is the Imam who is the head and leader of all believers.

[24] Among plants, some mild medicines have reached such a level of refinement and excellence that they have become antidotes (⟪ar:تریاقاً⟫) for those on the verge of death. Among them some cure chronic diseases while others are lower in degree. The peak and summit among those medicines point to the Imam; because his words become antidotes for the souls, and a means for the healing of its diseases and afflictions, as well as relief from death, illnesses, doubts and discords. The fatal poison and harmful effects that are to be found among medicines represent the opponents who forcefully usurp the position of the imams, peace be upon them. They destroy those who listen to them or accompany them or incline towards them, until the imam reaches them with the great antidote that rescues their souls from destruction. Likewise these opponents are like useless and worthless stones. It is for this reason that Allah, the Exalted, said:
⟪ar-quote:‏إِنَّكُمْ وَمَا تَعْبُدُونَ مِن دُونِ ٱللَّهِ حَصَبُ جَهَنَّمَ أَنتُمْ لَهَا وَرِدُونَ ‎⟫

Certainly! You and that which you are worshipping now besides Allah, are fuel for Hell!, you will enter it.

⟪ar-quote:‏فَإِن لَّمْ تَفْعَلُوا۟ وَلَن تَفْعَلُوا۟ فَٱتَّقُوا۟ ٱلنَّارَ ٱلَّتِى وَقُودُهَا ٱلنَّاسُ وَٱلْحِجَارَةُ ۖ أُعِدَّتْ لِلْكَفِرِينَ ‎⟫

But if you do it not, and you can never do it, then fear the Fire whose fuel is men and stones, prepared for the disbelievers.

[25] We also say that horse is the best among animals, eagle is the best among birds, while the lion is the king amongst beasts of prey. The differences in these various species of animals with regard to their disparity in strength, usefulness, and extent of their ability to accept training and in attaining the summit within their own species, points to the fact that there is a peak amongst the genus of animals. Therefore logically there must be a peak and summit amongst the human species, and that summit is the Imam, peace of Allah be upon him.

[26] We further say that some plants are sweet, delicious and appetizing, and people benefit from these, while others are bitter, having neither benefit nor delicacy. Some bear no fruit and have thorns that harm people. The sweet, pleasant ones are like the imams, and they are a symbol of their speech and knowledge that entice the soul and please the eyes. The bitter, putrid (Decaying or rotting and emitting a foul smell) and thorny ones symbolize the leaders of the literalists (⟪ar:اہل ظاہر⟫). For that reason Allah, the Exalted, said...

> ⟪quran 14:24-26⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَلَمْ تَرَ كَيْفَ ضَرَبَ ٱللَّهُ مَثَلًۭا كَلِمَةًۭ طَيِّبَةًۭ كَشَجَرَةٍۢ طَيِّبَةٍ أَصْلُهَا ثَابِتٌۭ وَفَرْعُهَا فِى ٱلسَّمَآءِ ‎ ‏تُؤْتِىٓ أُكُلَهَا كُلَّ حِينٍۭ بِإِذْنِ رَبِّهَا ۗ وَيَضْرِبُ ٱللَّهُ ٱلْأَمْثَالَ لِلنَّاسِ لَعَلَّهُمْ يَتَذَكَّرُونَ ‎ ‏وَمَثَلُ كَلِمَةٍ خَبِيثَةٍۢ كَشَجَرَةٍ خَبِيثَةٍ ٱجْتُثَّتْ مِن فَوْقِ ٱلْأَرْضِ مَا لَهَا مِن قَرَارٍۢ ‎⟫
> *See you not how Allah sets forth a parable? - A goodly word as a goodly tree, whose root is firmly fixed, and its branches (reach) to the sky (i.e. very high). Giving its fruit at all times, by the Leave of its Lord and Allah sets forth parables for mankind in order that they may remember. And the parable of an evil word is that of an evil tree uprooted from the surface of earth having no stability.*
> کیاتو نےنہیں دیکھا کہ اللہ نے کلمہ پاک کی ایک مثال بیان کی ہے گویا وہ ایک پاک درخت ہے کہ جس کی جڑ مضبوط اور اُس کی شاخ آسمان مین ہے وہ اپنے رب کے حکم سے ہر وقت اپنا پھل لاتا ہے اور اللہ لوگوں کے واسطے مثالیں بیان کرتا ہے تاکہ وہ سمجھیں اور ناپاک کلمہ کی مثال ایک ناپاک درخت کی سی ہے جو زمین کے اوپر ہی سے اکھاڑ لیا جائے اسے کچھ ٹھیراؤ نہیں ہے
> — **Quran 14:24-26 (inline widget)**

[40] We also say that wise men and men of insight, in buildIng the world, consider it to be similar to actions of Allah in His creation of the world, its environment and in preserving human welfare. When they see a good fertile land, they know that it will accept the planting of seeds and the growth of plants. When they see water in distant deep valleys or underground, they struggle to bring it forth from those valleys and from under the ground by digging canals and wells reverting water to those lands. They do not see any wisdom in leaving these good fertile lands unused and wasted or leaving aside the water unutilized, out of compassion for the creatures, as well as for safeguarding their welfare and the environment of the world. Likewise when the imams, peace be upon them, see people ready to accept the seed of wisdom and knowledge, although being very far from being able to receive it, the imams put great effort in digging canals through preparatory religious exercises on many an occasion. People would be perhaps unaware of the reason for that religious exercise until they realize its wisdom and become prepared and able to accept it. Perhaps, when the imams are unable to make them reach that level by exercise, they place the wisdom in many dense symbols, either in words or actions so that people can accept these symbols and gradually arrive at their meaning, and then the imams themselves elevate them to that level of understanding.

[41] In this manner, it is requisite to believe in the supreme leadership or the imamate of the imam of the time, and know that he is the head of the world and the vicegerent of Allah over His creation, and not to object to any of His commands, prohibitions, actions and teachings, and to know, in general, that all of that is wisdom and welfare for the creation. The correct aspect of that may be problematic for the believer at times, but in the end, its benefits will become clear to him, just as many of the things that were not known before become apparent and clear, and just as in much of the sharia, the faithful do not know the purpose of the Legislator and the wisdom in it and disapprove of that. Those whom Allah provides with the recognition of its meaning know the wisdom in it, just as many of those who see things in the world whose wisdom they do not understand think that there is no beneflt in it or in its creation, realize later that there is wisdom in it, which they are unable to deny. There are numerous things whose creation they [people] see as harmful and destructive, having no wisdom in it or any benefit, but when they realize its wisdom they become calm and content from their protest. Whoever recognizes the Wise One (الحکیم) and acknowledges that He is wise, it is inevitable that he knows and acknowledges that everything the Wise One does is full of wisdom and that He would not do anything that has no wisdom and that He would not command or prohibit or say anything except out of wisdom. Futile action is not permissible for the Wise One; if it were permissible for the Wise one to do, say, command or forbid anything that has no wisdom, then that would be a vain act which is not permissible for the Wise One. Whoever does anything whose doing or not doing is the same will be foolish and depart from the domain of wisdom.

[42] Further, if it is not permissible for the Wise One to perform an action whose existence or non-existence would be the same, how is it then possible for the imam to perform an action while wisdom is in another or in its opposite or that the welfare is in something other than it, while he, the imam, is absolutely wise and whose bestowal of wisdom on any one of his servants makes them wise? Whoever performs an action without wisdom and goodness, his action is corrupt and futile, and may Allah save us from those who believe that of the imam of the time. This would then mean that the individual has distanced himself from wisdom and if he departs from wisdom, he has thus departed from the domain of his imamate, and that is departure from the faith, may Allah protect us and all believers from all such doubt, ideads or belief as this. May He bestow upon us contentment and unquestioning submission (تسلیم).

[43] We also say that the freely-grazing livestock who have their own benefits and excellence must inevitably have a shepherd to tend to them, look after and protect them, and choose their feeding and drinking places, safeguarding them from thieves and beasts. If it were not for the fact that there was someone to undertake that, they would perish, being unable to manage their affairs by themselves, nor be able to defend themselves against beasts of prey, nor manage their affairs for their own good and well-being.

So, likewise, people are like sheep; if there is no Shepherd to protect them, they would perish. The imam is their shepherd safe guarding their worldly and religious affairs and preventing them from worldly and religious enemies. If they were to relinquish that role, not even two people would remain, nor would a single individual escape from punishment. It is in this manner that people in the countries are called subjects (رعایا), because they are under the custody of their shepherd, while the shepherd in reality is the Imam, the other claimants being wolves devouring the cattle.

[44] We maintain that the example of the world is that of the human body. If the body were to have no head, it would be a decayed cadaver of no use. Similarly, if there were no head, leader or master in the world, guiding the worldly and religious affairs, people would become beasts devouring each other. The world would not exist even for a single day and there would be no wisdom in the creation of the world. The imam is indeed the head of world, its leader and master.

[45] Further, we say that there are disparities (تفاوت) and differences in degrees of excellence (تفاضل) in the organs of the body; the foremost and the best among them is the head. It is in the head that the face is situated and by which each human being is recognized and distinguished from others. Among the internal organs, the best one is the brain, which is their chief, being the source of the intellect. So, likewise, the imam has a position in the world similar to the head and in relation to the organs, similar to the brain. Around him revolve all affairs of the creation just as all actions pertaining to the body revolve around the brain. Amongst the faculties in man and the spirits, the best is the intellect, and the imam is the Universal Intellect (عقل کلی) in the world from and in whom all people of the world become united.

[46] As we mentioned earlier, leadership in nature is present in everything. It is present in animals and in birds, such as the stallion protecting and disciplining its females. Thus the rooster protects its fowl, disciplining it. Every genus protects its young and children according to its capacity and defends its female, the weak among the genus as well as the female and the young ones according to their need for benefit and learning from those above. The crane obeys its leader and the bee obeys its chief.

[47] Indeed Allah, the Exalted, created the world and made the creatures as we mentioned earlier to a certain extent, according to this classification, disparity and difference in degrees of excellence, having more or less strength, nobility or inferiority so that they would know that in each species and genus there is a peak, summit and chief in nobility and merit. Likewise, it is necessary that the whole of mankind also have a peak and summit in nobility and merit that will be their leader and guide in the world. It has thus been shown that headship and leadership is necessary in nature and creation as well as within natural disposition and intuition, and that those who deny the revelation and religion are not able to deny the leadership, headship and authority of the world, either rationally or in witnessing it with their own eyes as it is obligatory and necessary. It is, therefore, mandatory that that leader should be the best among them all, the most noble, the most perfect, the most knowledgeable and the most pure according to the arguments that we have mentioned earlier from creation and nature, and that the foremost is the imam in everything as well as the chief and the head. The name supreme leader’ (الامام) cannot be placed on the one who is led (الامامون) nor the name ‘the excellent’ (الفاضل) on the ‘one preferred’ (المفضول), nor the name ‘one who supersedes’ (السابق) on ‘one who is preceded’ (المسبوق). Moreover, people from all communities and religions, as well as philosophers, atheists and those who deny Allah all attributes, affìrm that the leader of the world ought to be one who is the best among them, the most perfect in merit, and the most knowledgeable of all the people. There is no leader in the world of this description except for the imams, peace be upon them

[48] We also say that the philosophers divided politics or authority (سیاسۃ) into three categories: the authority of the individual (سیاست الخاصہ), the authority of the family (سیاست العامہ) and the authority of the general (سیاست الھامہ) The authority of the special is the governance of the individual himself and the authority of the family is the governance by a man of his family and dependents, while the authority of the general is governance of managing cities and provinces. The governance of the individual himself must be such that he stops his self from all vices, bad traits, bestial habits and blameworthy lusts, and that he governs his own self with the governance of a resolute person, his own self against his own self. Thus he punishes his soul when it errs through reproach and repentance, and rewards it when it does well by praise, happiness and by being consistent in doing that. The governance of one’s own family is that the individual manages his own household and his dependents by protecting their welfare, encouraging them to acquire virtues and pleasing character, punishing those who err by reprimanding and other such ways, and rewarding those who do good by praise and such other ways.

[49] The governance of generality is by man governing cities, protecting the welfare of their livelihood and preventing them from reprehensible morals and bad deeds. He protects all their positions and punishes those who err by reprimanding, while rewarding those who do well by praising, protecting and governing the affairs of their religion and the hereafter. This is what they call politics or authority; which is found neither in the world nor among those who [falsely] claim the imamate, nor among the rulers, and nor among their scholars. This attribute is not to be found anywhere except in the imams from the family of Mubammad, may Allah bless them, and there is no one in the world who is able to undertake this responsibility except them.

The philosophers agree that he who does not undertake the governance of his own self should not have the governance of managing his family. He who does not have a good management of his own family does not deserve governance of the generality; in any way. But the literalists (اہل الظاہر) and their rulers and scholars do not have this qualification. Those who sat in place of the imams and called themselves by their names cannot govern themselves, or their families, or the people; they are those whom we see today engaged in amusement, moral depravity and corruption. The qualification with which the philosophers describe the political leader is not held by any of their rulers. It is perhaps clear that the author of this classification aimed at encouraging obedience to the imam, for he described the imam by the attribute of the ruler so that they would look for a ruler with this qualification and description. Whoever does not have this description would not be accepted until they find the true imam.

[50] We also say that since people are ignorant at the time of their birth, having no knowledge, and as knowledge does not come to them from nature, nor does speech, therefore they need teaching. The proof that knowledge does not come forth from nature is that if knowledge did come from nature, then people would naturally be scholars and be able to speak naturally, just like the braying of donkeys and the barking of dogs, for it is obvious that they need no teaching for that. There is also no difference between the braying of donkeys and the barking of dogs in different parts of the world such as Hind, Sind, Rome and in the land of the Arabs. Further, if speech and knowledge came naturally, then, as mentioned earlier, it would certainly mean that people would need no teaching for that. People would be equal in that respect with no difference between one another, Just as mentioned earlier regarding the braying of donkeys being no different in different places. People, therefore, do need teaching, one learning from the other until they reach the one who has had no teaching from anyone but who received it through divine inspiration, not through teaching. This deficiency in people and their need for teaching necessitates a teacher, which in turn necessitates an ultimate end for the teachers, that is, the prophet and the imam, peace be upon them. That is among the most cogent or convincing proofs for the confirmation of the imamate and the prophethood.

[51] We also say that Allah, the Exalted, created human beings deficient and ignorant in order to make them accept knowledge and wisdom. If He had left them on their own there would be no obligation upon them and there would be no work, reward or punishment and there would have been no wisdom in creating them, Thus, when Allah inspired prophets and imams giving them wisdom and knowledge, they in turn informed mankind, explaining to them their guidance and their path to the Truth, imposing obligations, commands and prohibitions upon them. Further, if it were not for the imams, humanity would not be responsible and there would be no guarantor or proof Over them. Therefore, the imams are Allah’s proofs unto His creation at all times from the very beginning of their responsibility as well as when they fall into disagreement. If mankind fell into sectarian disagreement, arguing with one another by adducing a verse of the Quran, a tradition or analogical reasoning, then there would be no proof established for any of them against the other. if there were no imam in the world to save them from disagreement, confusion or perplexity and guiding them to the Truth, there would be no proof from Allah against the creatures, but indeed the proof would be from the creatures against Allah. For they would say: ‘We have not found anyone to guide us to the truth from falsehood. Therefore, through the imam the proof of Allah is established unto the people, just as Allah, the Exalted, said:

> ⟪quran 6:149⟫
> ⟪ar:‏قُلْ فَلِلَّهِ ٱلْحُجَّةُ ٱلْبَلِغَةُ ۖ فَلَوْ شَآءَ لَهَدَىٰكُمْ أَجْمَعِينَ ‎⟫
> *Say: "With Allah is the perfect proof and argument, (i.e.&nbsp;the Oneness of Allah, the sending of His Messengers and His Holy Books, etc.&nbsp;to mankind), had He so willed, He would indeed have guided you all."*
> کہہ دو پس اللہ کا الزام پورا ہو چکا پس اگر وہ چاہتا تو تم سب کو ہدایت کردیتا
> — **Quran 6:149 (inline widget)**

[52] We also say concerning the rules and regulations that are attributed to the sages, that the sages in reality are the imams, peace be upon them. From them people acquired the principles of all disciplines of knowledge and wisdom such as arithmetic and geometry. There is a purpose for each one of them and an end which points to the imam. The end among the geometric shapes such as squares, triangles, arcs and all other shapes is the circle. The circle is the best and most perfect of them all. It is the foundation of all shapes from which it is possible to form the square, the triangle and the arc. When the circle is divided, a square emerges and arcs remain on the edges. If we take the horizontal and the vertical lines, there will be four triangles; all other shapes are derived from the circle and all shapes are contained within it. The position of shapes is similar to the world and the creation. Among the shapes, the circle is made a proof and evidence for the imam, who is the circle of the religion (دائرہ الدین), and all the hudud (ranks of the hierarchy) are contained within his command and prohibition while they all benefit from him. The circle is in no need of any shape, which all other shapes need it, just as the imam is in no need of other ranks in the hierarchy in His age and time, whereas all the ranks need him; he encompasses them all.

[53] We also say that the origin and cause of numbers is the number one. It is the most perfect of all numbers, being independent of the number two and what is above, up to a thousand. The thousand and what is below need the number one. The imam is the one who is unique in his age and time; all ranks of the hierarchy need him while he is independent of everyone. If some people think of the number one as an indication of the Creator of the creatures, then this assumption is wrong because the number one is the cause of mathematics and the foundation of numbers, while the number two is one plus one and similarly the number three. But one is indeed the imam in his rank and position, being unique. No one else among the creatures in his age and time share his position.

[54] We also say that the dot, which the mathematicians mention has no parts to it and is the origin of the line, its surface and the body, is an indication for the imam whose rank or status no one can attain and who cannot be truly recognized. No one can describe his attributes properly; rather they attest their own weakness.

[55] Further, we say that among all the days Saturday is the most important and amongst all the months, Ramadan is the best. Within the hours, there is one hour in which the supplication (دعا) is answered. Every genus and species in the world, be it created or posited (put forward as a basis of argument) certainly has a peak and a summit in nobility and merit, which none can attain. That points to the imam as we mentioned earlier. If we were to mention everything that should be entered in this chapter, this treatise would go beyond its limit. What we have mentioned should suffice for those who contemplate, and it will be possible for him to make analogical deductions from the principles and branches we have mentioned. However, we shall mention, by adducing evidence [aspects] from the obligatory religious duties (فرائض) and their structure, some points in brevity.

[56] We also say that in the ritual prayer and its arrangement, its prescribed standing and direction of the qibla, and in the standing of the imam in front of all the rows, are a powerful indication for affirming the imamate. That is because the Prophet may Allah bless him, first ordered the Muslims to face the qibla. The qibla is derived from qabala, which means 'Face-to-face' and whoever faces it, points his face directly to it, and that is the imam. It is said that to be before mean precedence. That is the opposite of back, behind and after. The word Imam derives from one meaning and the imam of the prayer is thus called an imam for this reason because he precedes the worshippers. The indication to the qibla is an indication for the imam, and [the Prophet] commanded people to follow and obey him in all forms of worship and to accept his direction. When a man faces what is in front of him during prayers, he is facing the qibla with respect to the imam in all his worship and obedience to him, Then, if an individual’s prayer is with his imam as the Prophet mentioned that the congregational prayer is equal to 27  prayers said by an individual on his own—its merit is because it is with the imam while he is facing him, following him and being led by him in intention and action. That is an indication that the entire aspect ofl obedience is being led by the supreme imam (امام الاعظم)—guided, followed and led by him so that obedience has excellence. Then the Prophet, may Allah bless him, ordered them to align in rows, so that there was no difference between anyone in their arising; this is an indication that it is not permissible for the hearts of those who are led and guided by the imam to be different, and nor should this be the case in their actions or their speech.

[57] The Prophet, may Allah bless him, ordered them to follow the imam of the prayers, even if the recitation, arising or prostration became prolonged and not to go against him in gestures or in intention. This was the case even when the worshipper agrees only with the imam’s action and not his intention, his prayer would still not be accepted. If one who is led is negligent, the imam removes his negligence. It is evident from all this that if the obedience of the partial (جزو) imam, who is not an absolute imam, is made obligatory, and the reward of that worship is increased, then how about the obedience of the supreme (اعظم) imam who is an imam in all revealed law (شریعۃ) and esoteric interpretation (تاویل)? Further, if it is not permissible to oppose the imam in any of the prayer actions, then how can it be permissible to oppose the supreme imam in his commands and prohibitions in the life of a believer? The believer remains forever under the patronage  of the da’wa in the prayer as long as he is induded in the allegiance (ولایا) of the imam. If he opposes him in an action, intention or in decision, he will indeed have anulled his prayers and departed from the norm of the worshipper, just as when the worshipper resolves to oppose the imam, his prayer, bowing، prostration, standing and sitting are worthless, and his action is  futile and he must restart the prayer. Then how about the obedience to the supreme imam, which Allah has made absolutely obligatory? The Prophet has said: ‘The imam is the one responsible' [for those who follow him] and it certainly does not mean the imam of the prayer, for he requires someone who can vouch for him. Indeed, the indication is to the supreme imam, peace be upon him, who guarantees the purification of those led by him from doubt, suspicion, confusion, forgetfulness, and guarantees his salvation as long as he is guided by him, following him. The Prophet ìndicated the position of the imam preceding everyone and commanded them not to compete with the imam in the recitation of the Quran, and he said ‘When he prostrates, you should prostrate, when he bows you bow and when he recites you listen, and when he says the salutations (تسلیم) then you should say it too.

[58] All these are indications for the obedience to the imams, peace be upon them, and for their glorffication in all matters, and the permanence of their position in their time, the necessity of obeying them, and the submission (tastim) of the command (الامر) when he condudes his affair to whomsoever he submits it. Even if there were no proof for the imam and for his obedience in the sharia except for in the prayer, that would be sufficient. Thus, the Prophet explained that the imam absolves worshippers from their negligence in prayer, which means that the imam relieves their slips, and seeks forgiveness for them. As Allah, the Exalted, said:

> ⟪quran 4:64⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَمَآ أَرْسَلْنَا مِن رَّسُولٍ إِلَّا لِيُطَاعَ بِإِذْنِ ٱللَّهِ ۚ وَلَوْ أَنَّهُمْ إِذ ظَّلَمُوٓا۟ أَنفُسَهُمْ جَآءُوكَ فَٱسْتَغْفَرُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ وَٱسْتَغْفَرَ لَهُمُ ٱلرَّسُولُ لَوَجَدُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ تَوَّابًۭا رَّحِيمًۭا ‎⟫
> *We sent no Messenger, but to be obeyed by Allah's Leave.&nbsp;If they (hypocrites), when they had been unjust to themselves, had come to you (Muhammad PBUH) and begged Allah's Forgiveness, and the Messenger had begged forgiveness for them: indeed, they would have found Allah All-Forgiving (One Who accepts repentance), Most Merciful.*
> اورہم نے کبھی کوئی رسول نہیں بھیجا مگر اسی واسطے کہ اللہ کے حکم سے اس کی تابعداری کی جائے اور جب انہوں نے اپنے نفسوں پر ظلم کیا تھا تیرے پاس آتے پھر اللہ سے معافی مانگتے اور رسول بھی اُن کی معافی کی درخواست کرتا تو یقیناًیہ اللہ کو بخشنے والا رحم کرنے والا پاتے
> — **Quran 4:64 (inline widget)**

If the imam were to remove forgiveness and acceptance of repentance from this community, they would surely perish for they are most in need of forgiveness. Rather, all that remains in effect, in every age and time, for those who come to the imam, is for the imam to seek forgiveness for them, and Allah will forgive them just as he did for those people.

[59] We also say that the Friday prayer is not acceptable without the sermon (خطبا) delivered on the pulpits (منابر). People pray behind the imam so that they realize that obedience to the imam is not lifted from any created being anywhere. Furthermore the pilgrimage in its entirety is a proof for the affirmation of the imamate. The pilgrimage is an intention, and the intention must be for a known matter so that when the intention is mentioned with full knowledge (معرفہ) it becomes a known intention that needs no explanation. That is an indication for the intention towards the Imam. The Ka'ba in some esoteric interpretations, is a proof for the imam (حجت الامام). Its being placed in a desert with no civilization around it so that it can only be reached with great difficulty, and its location in a place that has no planting or trees deprived of  worldly benefit are such so that the worshippers should know that what is symbolized by it (ممثول) also can be attained only by great effort and difficulty as well as injury from enemies. They should also know that aiming for the imam and seeking him must not be for worldly purpose, greed, pleasure or worldly dignity but visiting the imam must only be out of pure faith. If he faces hardship, tiredness, attacks from enemies, fatigue or other such things, then his heart must not constrict, but he must patiently endure. Then he will see and recognize as such in its symbol (مثل), which is the pilgrimage. Then its circurnambulation (طواف), touching or accepting it (استلام), the indication of it, the running to it, the throwing of stones, the wearing of white garments (احرام) and giving up of perfume and sex, all that is an indication for the affirmation of the imamate and obedience to him in all different conditions, seeking guidance and protection of their souls while discarding reprehensible doctrines and corrupt beliefs.

[60] We also say that the most emphatic proof for the necessity of the imamate is in the obligation of alms (zakat), in its religious duties, its safekeeping and in its distribution. That is because Allah, the Exalted, commanded the Prophet to take almsgiving (صدقہ) from them when He said:

> ⟪quran 9:103⟫
> ⟪ar:‏خُذْ مِنْ أَمْوَلِهِمْ صَدَقَةًۭ تُطَهِّرُهُمْ وَتُزَكِّيهِم بِهَا وَصَلِّ عَلَيْهِمْ ۖ إِنَّ صَلَوٰتَكَ سَكَنٌۭ لَّهُمْ ۗ وَٱللَّهُ سَمِيعٌ عَلِيمٌ ‎⟫
> *Take Sadaqah (alms) from their wealth in order to purify them and sanctify them with it, and invoke Allah for them. Verily! Your invocations are a source of security for them, and Allah is All-Hearer, All-Knower.*
> ان کے مالوں میں سے زکواة لے کہ اس سے ان کے ظاہر کو پاک اور ان کے باطن کو صاف کر دے اورانہیں دعا دے بے شک تیری دعا ان کے لیے تسکین ہے اوراللہ سننے والا جاننے والا ہے
> — **Quran 9:103 (inline widget)**

Then the Prophet explained the obligations of zakaat, its amount and how it should be collected. He himself collected it until they knew how it should be given and how it should be collected. He who sat in place of the imams also collected the zakat, claiming that collecting alms belonged to him and arguing against the umma with this verse and through the actions of Allah’s Messenger, may Allah bless him. He waged war against the Banu Hanifa for that reason and killed them. Those who sat in place of the imams after him also collected the alms until this matter reathed their leaders who took offence [to this], kept the alms money for themselves and prevented it being collected on behalf of the imam.

Is it any wonder then to see the condition of this community? They affirm that this verse is abrogating (ناسخ) in judgement and recitation, yet it is not abrogated (منسوخ) and that the Prophetic sunna continues to require collection of alms. How did they make allowance for changing the rule in the verse and of Allah’s command and changing the sunna [of the Prophet] and the sunna of those whose imainate they claim? The only intention for changing that was their denial of the imams’ status and the existence of imamate in the Prophet’s family (اہل بیت), may Allah bless him and his family. Allah, the Exalted, had explained in regard to alms (zakaat) and the manner of collecting it, the position of the imamate and the imams by forbidding , sadaqa to the Prophet so that they would not accuse him of taking them. Likewise, He forbade them to the Prophet’s family so that they would know that the imam among them is the one who takes the position of the Prophet, may Allah bless him and his family, in collecting the alms, and that they [the imamsj are trustworthy in this regard.

[61] If people had been entrusted to discharge the duty of almsgiving and its distribution themselves, Allah would have commanded them to do so, just as He commanded them with regard to prayer, fasting and other obligatory duties. But He did not order them to distribute the sadaqa, instead He commanded the Prophet, may Allah bless him, to do so. If it were permissible for the people to do it themselves, then that would have been permissible during the Prophet’s time when they were far more steadfast in religion, in their certainty of faith, as well as in having more integrity. How is it then that later on they have become trustees of  almsgiving? Why is it also permissible for them that the prayer, which is more preferable than almsgiving, is to be behind their imams and such other duties, but that it is not acceptable to give their imams alms? Further, why is it that they are trustworthy with regard to shedding of blood and sexual offences and with respect to all other aspects of property and yet not be reliable and trustworthy with regard to alms? If people were truthful regarding what they say about their imams being untrustworthy with regard to alms, then they are not actually imams but embezzlers. If they are embezzlers, it is not permissible to pray behind them or for them to conduct any other duties such as jihad and pilgrimage or give rulings in respect to sexual offences, shedding of blood and property. If these people are lying in what they say and claim, then their scholars who put forward religious opinions (فتوا) in that regard are liars too, since they are those who bear witness to their leadership, and the testimony of liars is not acceptable. Allah, the Exalted, also commanded the Prophet, may Allah bless him and his family, to purify the believers and pray for them when He said

> ⟪quran 9:103⟫
> ⟪ar:‏خُذْ مِنْ أَمْوَلِهِمْ صَدَقَةًۭ تُطَهِّرُهُمْ وَتُزَكِّيهِم بِهَا وَصَلِّ عَلَيْهِمْ ۖ إِنَّ صَلَوٰتَكَ سَكَنٌۭ لَّهُمْ ۗ وَٱللَّهُ سَمِيعٌ عَلِيمٌ ‎⟫
> *Take Sadaqah (alms) from their wealth in order to purify them and sanctify them with it, and invoke Allah for them. Verily! Your invocations are a source of security for them, and Allah is All-Hearer, All-Knower.*
> ان کے مالوں میں سے زکواة لے کہ اس سے ان کے ظاہر کو پاک اور ان کے باطن کو صاف کر دے اورانہیں دعا دے بے شک تیری دعا ان کے لیے تسکین ہے اوراللہ سننے والا جاننے والا ہے
> — **Quran 9:103 (inline widget)**

Thus, He made purilication for them and prayer upon them a means of their tranquility; and the prayer was compensation for the alms He took from them.

If He had given compensation for almsgiving to the people present in the time of the Prophet, may Allah bless him, and had not given it to those who came after them, even though they are more in need of it than those present in the time of the Prophet, may Allah bless him, then that would indeed be injustice against those who came after that age. Allah is above injustice with regard to His worshippers and He, may His name be exalted, does not command an obligation and provide a compensation (انعام) for it in this world or the here after, except that He made the compensation in general. Rather, the aspect of purification, prayer, and tranquillity perpetually remain with whosoever comes to the imam and gives alias (zakãt) from his property, be it in public or in private. The imam then purifies him and prays for him. If the Imam were in fact necessary only for this, then that would be sufficient. His distribution of alms to those entitled to it is because he knows those to whom it ought to be given and those for whom it is not permissible to be given and he also knows when there is no one in a category of people entitled to alms for the portion that ought to be given. The imam [therefore] is the one who protects the treasury of the Muslims, distributing it according to the needs of religion and time.

[62] We also say that jihad is one of the principles of religion and that it is only permissible to wage war under the banner of an imam. No command for waging war can be established except from the imam, the reason being that the imam first needs to protect the treasury (بیت المال) of the Muslims which is under his guarantee, and protect the border towns as well as the Muslim arms and rescue the Muslim prisoners of war from the hands of the infidels by giving ransom. Moreover, it is only permissible to send out an army under a commander appointed by the imam or by someone appointed by the imam. The imam is more knowledeable of the times of peace and agreement or treaties, and it is he who concludes the treaties. Then when he takes the prisoners of war, he knows whom to forgive, whom to seek ransom for and whom to put to death. He is more knowledgeable about the ways in which to take the land tax (kharãj) and money so that it is a means of benefit and support for the Muslims. The imam also knows the rebel and it is also through the imam that a party becomes the party of the truth because it is with him. The rebel is the one who departs from the obedience of the imam, and then it is permissible for the imam to wage war and fight, or to make peace and armistice (truce). Shafi said: ‘If it were not for the Commander of the Faithful, ‘Ali ibne Abu Talib, peace be upon him, we would not have known how to wage war against rebels nor would we have been able to tell the difference between the rebel and the rightful believers.

[63] Thereafter, there is the fifth (khums) that Allah gave specifically to the Prophet’s family and to the imams in place of the alms (sadaqa) which he forbade them. All benefits from alms and zakaat as well as their requirement are linked to the imam. Furthermore, there are the Eid feasts and the month of Ramadan, where the imam preserves and accepts the testimony of the witness, and from among the opponents, whether they hold that fasting and breaking of the fast is done by sighting the moon or by the one appointed by the imam. The two feast prayers and the Friday prayer are not acceptable in congregation without a sermon (khuthã) from the imam and his presence or by someone who the imam appoints, even four people in the congregation are reduced to two because of the imam’s sermon.

[64] Then the execution of legal punishments (حدود): Only the imam or the one whom the imam designates may carry Out legal punishments. For example, cutting off hands, flogging, stoning, imprisonment, indemnity for injuries Çarsh a1-jirüãt) and judgement concerning them can only be carried out by orders of the imam. If

these rules were the only proof for the imamate in the Messenger’s family, then that would be sufficient. For the opponents agree that whoever has no authority (waiãya) cannot be allowed to give judgement on legal punishments. Therefore, if a man sees another killing someone unjustly, it is not up to him to kill that person. And if he were to see someone stealing, it is not for him to cut his hand off, stone him or do other such things. The extent of this goes so far that most people agree that it is not for the slave’s owner to carry out legal punishments or to chastise him; only the imam should chastise him and carry out legal punishments. It is not possible to abolish legal punishments because if they were to be abolished, people would perish and countries would be ruined. If people were allowed to carry out legal punishments, everyone would intend to kill or hit and then claim that the person had killed someone else or stolen money that necessitated him to carry out the legal punishment. Yet how can someone who himself requires twenty legal punishments every day, rule on legal punishments, and how can he be permitted to carry them out? If he were allowed to

do those, then that would certainly be permissible for every oppressor or rebel. It would mean perdition for the people. Rather, when a rebellious party carries out legal punishments and destroys peoples lives and the imam has power over them, he fines them for whatever damage they caused to the righteous party, preventing the wrong doers from destroying the people and damaging their property; Then, they claim that all was done according to a legal rule enjoined upon them. But Allah, the Exalted, has clarified this in His words:

> ⟪quran 2:44⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ أَتَأْمُرُونَ ٱلنَّاسَ بِٱلْبِرِّ وَتَنسَوْنَ أَنفُسَكُمْ وَأَنتُمْ تَتْلُونَ ٱلْكِتَبَ ۚ أَفَلَا تَعْقِلُونَ ‎⟫
> *Enjoin you Al-Birr (piety and righteousness and each and every act of obedience to Allah) on the people and you forget (to practise it) yourselves, while you recite the Scripture [the Taurat (Torah)]! Have you then no sense?*
> کیا لوگوں کو تم نیکی کا حکم کرتے ہو اور اپنے آپ کو بھول جاتے ہو حالانکہ تم کتاب پڑھتے ہو پھر کیوں نہیں سمجھتے
> — **Quran 2:44 (inline widget)**

Allah, the Exalted, warned that whoever needs to be commanded to do good and be prevented from evil is not allowed to command people to do good and forbid evil. Allah has also explained in another verse that ‘enjoining good and forbidding evil’ (al-atnr bi’l-ma’rufwa nahy ‘an al-rnunkar), is a duty of the imams, peace be upon them, when He said: ‘You are the best community (umma) that has been raised for the people. You enjoin good conduct and forbid evil. They are the equitable leaders (aimma al-wasat) who are witnesses over the people. How can one command good if he does not practice it himself and how can he forbid evil if he himself loves evil and commits it every day a hundred times? How is it permissible for their imams when they commit the very things that necessitate legal punishment every day, that is, their acts of lust and desire? And when they draw close to themselves those who love doing that and who join them in it? How can they forbid such acts while they see them as elegant. victorious, convivial, charming and refined? Whoever does not join them in drinking and debauchery, they will neither draw him near, nor employ him, for he would be disagreeable to them. Is that not a lesson for those who are led by them and an incitement for them to tread the path of corruption and debauchery?
